## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relation linking stress to strain and temperature. In materials science, stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic hardening laws, while temperature introduces thermal softening, modulus reduction, and potentially thermally-activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elasticity with T-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening, Ramberg-Osgood style)
- Johnson-Cook (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (power-law thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening + thermal softening)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) (polynomial T-dependence of modulus)
- Zerilli-Armstrong (BCC-type): sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (thermally-activated flow stress)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/hyperbolic sine creep law)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon * T (quadratic with cross-term)
- Rubber elasticity (neo-Hookean with T): sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) (entropic elasticity, stress proportional to T)
- Ludwik-Hollomon with T: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * T (additive thermal correction to power-law hardening)
- Swift law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (shifted power law with linear T factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening typically appears as a multiplicative factor decreasing with T: (1 - c*T), exp(-c*T), or T**(-c) — separable from strain dependence
- Entropic elasticity (rubber-like materials) shows stress proportional to absolute temperature: sigma ~ T * f(epsilon)
- Strain hardening saturation suggests exponential approach forms: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally-activated deformation mechanisms produce Arrhenius-type terms: exp(-c0 / T) or exp(c0 * T), reflecting activation energy barriers
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects (sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T)) is common in constitutive models, reflecting separable hardening and softening
- A shift in strain origin (epsilon + c0)**c1 (Swift-type) indicates pre-strain or initial dislocation density effects
- Hyperbolic sine (sinh) appears in high-temperature creep/flow models bridging power-law and exponential regimes
- Polynomial strain terms with odd symmetry (epsilon, epsilon**3) arise in nonlinear elasticity where stress must be an odd function of strain
